\begin{lemma}[Higher-order smoothed Mellin projector]
\label{lem:higher-order-smoothed-mellin-projector}
Fix an integer \(M\ge 1\). Let \(\phi_M\in C_c^\infty(\mathbf R)\) be even and
satisfy
\[
\int_{\mathbf R}\phi_M(u)\,du=1,
\qquad
\int_{\mathbf R}u^{2\ell}\phi_M(u)\,du=0
\quad (1\le \ell\le M-1).
\]
Define its bilateral Laplace transform by
\[
\widehat\phi_M(w):=\int_{\mathbf R}\phi_M(u)e^{wu}\,du.
\]
For \(\eta>0\), define
\[
(\mathcal P_{N,Q,\eta}^{(M)}F)
:=
\sum_{j=1}^N a_j^{(N)}
\int_{\mathbf R}\phi_M(u)\,
F\!\left(\frac{j}{Q^2}+\eta u\right)\,du,
\]
whenever \(F\) is holomorphic on a neighborhood of the integration region.

Then:

\begin{enumerate}
\item for every exponential mode \(F(s)=e^{zs}\),
\[
\mathcal P_{N,Q,\eta}^{(M)}(e^{zs})
=
\widehat\phi_M(\eta z)\,\widehat\mu_{N,Q}(z),
\qquad
\widehat\mu_{N,Q}(z)=\sum_{j=1}^N a_j^{(N)}e^{zj/Q^2};
\]

\item one has
\[
\widehat\phi_M(0)=1,
\qquad
\widehat\phi_M^{(k)}(0)=0
\quad (1\le k\le 2M-1);
\]

\item the smoothed symbol preserves the exact low odd-jet annihilation:
\[
\partial_z^{\,2r+1}\!\bigl(\widehat\phi_M(\eta z)\widehat\mu_{N,Q}(z)\bigr)\Big|_{z=0}=0
\qquad (0\le r\le N-2);
\]

\item if \(F\) is holomorphic on a neighborhood \(\Omega\) containing all points
\[
\frac{j}{Q^2}+\eta u
\qquad
(1\le j\le N,\ u\in \operatorname{supp}\phi_M),
\]
then
\[
\bigl|\mathcal P_{N,Q,\eta}^{(M)}F-\mathcal P_{N,Q}F\bigr|
\le
\frac{\eta^{2M}}{(2M)!}\,(2N-1)\,m_{2M}(\phi_M)\,
\sup_{\Omega}|F^{(2M)}|,
\]
where
\[
m_{2M}(\phi_M):=\int_{\mathbf R}|u|^{2M}|\phi_M(u)|\,du.
\]
\end{enumerate}
\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
For \(F(s)=e^{zs}\),
\[
\mathcal P_{N,Q,\eta}^{(M)}(e^{zs})
=
\sum_{j=1}^N a_j^{(N)}e^{zj/Q^2}
\int_{\mathbf R}\phi_M(u)e^{\eta zu}\,du
=
\widehat\phi_M(\eta z)\,\widehat\mu_{N,Q}(z),
\]
which proves the first statement.

Since \(\phi_M\) is even, all odd moments vanish. By the imposed even-moment
conditions, one also has
\[
\int_{\mathbf R}u^k\phi_M(u)\,du=0
\qquad (1\le k\le 2M-1).
\]
Differentiating \(\widehat\phi_M\) at \(0\) gives
\[
\widehat\phi_M^{(k)}(0)=\int_{\mathbf R}u^k\phi_M(u)\,du,
\]
so
\[
\widehat\phi_M(0)=1,
\qquad
\widehat\phi_M^{(k)}(0)=0
\quad (1\le k\le 2M-1).
\]
This proves the second statement.

By Lemma~\ref{lem:n-point-mellin-symbol},
\[
\widehat\mu_{N,Q}(0)=1,
\qquad
\partial_z^{\,2r+1}\widehat\mu_{N,Q}(0)=0
\quad (0\le r\le N-2).
\]
Applying Leibniz' rule to
\(\widehat\phi_M(\eta z)\widehat\mu_{N,Q}(z)\) shows that all odd derivatives
up to order \(2N-3\) vanish at \(z=0\), proving the third statement.

For the quantitative comparison, expand \(F\) to order \(2M-1\) at \(j/Q^2\):
\[
F\!\left(\frac{j}{Q^2}+\eta u\right)
=
\sum_{k=0}^{2M-1}
\frac{(\eta u)^k}{k!}\,
F^{(k)}\!\left(\frac{j}{Q^2}\right)
+
\frac{(\eta u)^{2M}}{(2M)!}\,F^{(2M)}(\xi_{j,u})
\]
for some \(\xi_{j,u}\in\Omega\). Integrating against \(\phi_M\), all terms of
order \(1\) through \(2M-1\) vanish by the moment conditions, while the
constant term survives because \(\int\phi_M=1\). Hence
\[
\int_{\mathbf R}\phi_M(u)\,
F\!\left(\frac{j}{Q^2}+\eta u\right)\,du
-
F\!\left(\frac{j}{Q^2}\right)
=
\frac{\eta^{2M}}{(2M)!}
\int_{\mathbf R}\phi_M(u)\,u^{2M}F^{(2M)}(\xi_{j,u})\,du.
\]
Summing against \(a_j^{(N)}\) and using
Lemma~\ref{lem:n-point-coefficients},
\[
\sum_{j=1}^N |a_j^{(N)}|=2N-1,
\]
gives the claimed bound.
\qedhere
\end{proof}

\begin{proposition}[Higher-order smoothed comparison for the corrected \(N\)-point zeta scalar]
\label{prop:higher-order-smoothed-zeta-n-point-comparison}
Fix an integer \(M\ge 1\), and let \(\phi_M\in C_c^\infty(\mathbf R)\) be even,
normalized, and moment-corrected as in
Lemma~\ref{lem:higher-order-smoothed-mellin-projector}. Set
\[
U_M:=\sup\{|u|:u\in \operatorname{supp}\phi_M\},
\qquad
m_{2M}(\phi_M):=\int_{\mathbf R}|u|^{2M}|\phi_M(u)|\,du.
\]
Fix \(0<\alpha<\rho_0\), let
\[
N=\lfloor \alpha Q\rfloor,
\]
and assume
\[
0<\eta\le \frac{\rho_0-\alpha}{2U_M\,Q}.
\]
Define
\[
H_{m,\eta}^{(M)}(s):=\int_{\mathbf R}\phi_M(u)\,H_m(s+\eta u)\,du,
\]
and
\[
\Xi_{\zeta,\eta}^{(N,M)}(m)
:=
\sum_{j=1}^N a_j^{(N)}\,H_{m,\eta}^{(M)}\!\left(\frac{j}{Q^2}\right).
\]
Then:

\begin{enumerate}
\item \(H_{m,\eta}^{(M)}\) is odd and holomorphic on
\[
|s|<\frac{\rho_{M,\eta}}{Q},
\qquad
\rho_{M,\eta}:=\rho_0-U_M\eta Q>\alpha;
\]

\item one has
\[
|\Xi_{\zeta,\eta}^{(N,M)}(m)|
\ll_{\phi_M,\rho_0,\alpha}
\frac{L(m)S(m)^2}{Q}\,
e^{-\delta_*(\alpha,\rho_{M,\eta})Q};
\]

\item the smoothed and discrete \(N\)-point scalars satisfy
\[
|\Xi_{\zeta,\eta}^{(N,M)}(m)-\Xi_{\zeta}^{(N)}(m)|
\le
C_{\partial}(\rho_0)\,(2N-1)\,m_{2M}(\phi_M)\,
\left(\frac{2}{\rho_0-\alpha}\right)^{2M}
\eta^{2M}Q^{2M-3}\,
L(m)S(m)^2,
\]
and hence
\[
|\Xi_{\zeta,\eta}^{(N,M)}(m)-\Xi_{\zeta}^{(N)}(m)|
\ll_{\phi_M,\rho_0,\alpha}
(\eta Q)^{2M}\,\frac{L(m)S(m)^2}{Q^2}.
\]
\end{enumerate}
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
The proof of oddness and holomorphy is identical to that of
Proposition~\ref{prop:smoothed-zeta-n-point-comparison}, with \(\phi\) replaced
by \(\phi_M\). Likewise, on \(|s|=\rho_{M,\eta}/Q\),
\[
|H_{m,\eta}^{(M)}(s)|
\le
\|\phi_M\|_{L^1}\,C_{\partial}(\rho_0)\,\frac{L(m)S(m)^2}{Q^3}.
\]
Therefore the proof of
Corollary~\ref{cor:optimized-zeta-cancellation-depth} applies verbatim with
\(\rho_0\) replaced by \(\rho_{M,\eta}\), giving the stated exponential bound.

For the comparison estimate,
\[
\Xi_{\zeta,\eta}^{(N,M)}(m)-\Xi_{\zeta}^{(N)}(m)
=
\bigl(\mathcal P_{N,Q,\eta}^{(M)}-\mathcal P_{N,Q}\bigr)H_m.
\]
Apply Lemma~\ref{lem:higher-order-smoothed-mellin-projector} with \(F=H_m\).
Exactly as in the proof of
Proposition~\ref{prop:smoothed-zeta-n-point-comparison}, all relevant points
lie at distance at least
\[
\frac{\rho_0-\alpha}{2Q}
\]
from the boundary circle \(|s|=\rho_0/Q\). Hence Cauchy's derivative estimate
and Proposition~\ref{prop:boundary-estimate} give
\[
\sup_{\Omega}|H_m^{(2M)}|
\le
(2M)!\,C_{\partial}(\rho_0)\,
\left(\frac{2Q}{\rho_0-\alpha}\right)^{2M}
\frac{L(m)S(m)^2}{Q^3}.
\]
Substituting this into Lemma~\ref{lem:higher-order-smoothed-mellin-projector}
yields
\[
|\Xi_{\zeta,\eta}^{(N,M)}(m)-\Xi_{\zeta}^{(N)}(m)|
\le
C_{\partial}(\rho_0)\,(2N-1)\,m_{2M}(\phi_M)\,
\left(\frac{2}{\rho_0-\alpha}\right)^{2M}
\eta^{2M}Q^{2M-3}\,
L(m)S(m)^2,
\]
as claimed. Since \(N\asymp Q\), the final big-Oh form follows.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Saturation at the natural \(Q^{-1}\) smoothing scale]
\label{rem:higher-order-smoothing-saturation}
Proposition~\ref{prop:higher-order-smoothed-zeta-n-point-comparison} shows that
higher-order moment correction improves the comparison error to order
\(2M\), but under the largest admissible smoothing scale
\[
\eta\asymp Q^{-1},
\]
one still has
\[
|\Xi_{\zeta,\eta}^{(N,M)}(m)-\Xi_{\zeta}^{(N)}(m)|
\ll
\frac{L(m)S(m)^2}{Q^2}.
\]
Thus higher-order smoothing does not improve the \(Q\)-power at the natural
admissible scale; its gain is in canonicity and in the ability to make the
smoothed projector arbitrarily close to the discrete one once one works at a
smaller scale. For example, if
\[
\eta=Q^{-1-\sigma}
\qquad (\sigma>0),
\]
then
\[
|\Xi_{\zeta,\eta}^{(N,M)}(m)-\Xi_{\zeta}^{(N)}(m)|
\ll
Q^{-2-2M\sigma}\,L(m)S(m)^2.
\]
\end{remark}

\end{remark}

\end{remark}

\begin{proposition}[Positive smoothing preserves the real kernel profile]
\label{prop:smoothed-real-kernel-profile}
Let \(\psi\in C_c^\infty(\mathbf R)\) be even, nonnegative, and normalized by
\[
\int_{\mathbf R}\psi(u)\,du=1.
\]
Set
\[
U_\psi:=\sup\{|u|:u\in \operatorname{supp}\psi\}.
\]
For \(x>N+\eta Q^2U_\psi\), define the smoothed real profile
\[
\kappa_{N,\eta}^{\psi}(x)
:=
\int_{\mathbf R}\psi(u)\,\kappa_N(x+\eta Q^2u)\,du,
\]
where
\[
\kappa_N(x):=x\,\frac{\Gamma(x-N)}{\Gamma(x+N+1)}
=\frac{1}{\prod_{j=1}^N(x^2-j^2)}.
\]
Then
\[
\kappa_{N,\eta}^{\psi}(x)>0
\qquad\text{and}\qquad
\frac{d}{dx}\kappa_{N,\eta}^{\psi}(x)<0
\]
for all \(x>N+\eta Q^2U_\psi\).
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
For \(x>N+\eta Q^2U_\psi\) and \(u\in \operatorname{supp}\psi\), one has
\[
x+\eta Q^2u>N.
\]
By Proposition~\ref{prop:exact-kernel-real-profile},
\[
\kappa_N(x+\eta Q^2u)>0
\qquad\text{and}\qquad
\kappa_N'(x+\eta Q^2u)<0.
\]
Since \(\psi\ge 0\) and \(\int \psi=1\), averaging preserves positivity:
\[
\kappa_{N,\eta}^{\psi}(x)>0.
\]
Differentiating under the integral sign gives
\[
\frac{d}{dx}\kappa_{N,\eta}^{\psi}(x)
=
\int_{\mathbf R}\psi(u)\,\kappa_N'(x+\eta Q^2u)\,du<0.
\]
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Smoothed real profile]
\label{rem:smoothed-real-kernel-profile}
Proposition~\ref{prop:smoothed-real-kernel-profile} shows that nonnegative
smoothing preserves the qualitative real-axis behavior of the exact kernel:
positivity and strict monotonic decay survive averaging. Thus the Mellin-side
smoothing introduced later does not destroy the basic real-profile structure of
the \(N\)-point kernel.
\end{remark}

These are the remaining worthwhile insertions on this line.

What they add:

    a genuinely higher-order smooth Mellin projector package;

    a higher-order smoothed zeta comparison theorem;

    an explicit remark explaining the saturation phenomenon;

    and a small but clean theorem that positive smoothing preserves real-axis kernel monotonicity.

That is about as much as I think is worth squeezing out of this Connes/Mellin direction before returns really flatten.

ok, where might we push next in terms of importing existing RH understanding?

I’m going to answer this as “what existing RH machinery is most plausibly importable into your current architecture,” not as a generic list of famous approaches. The useful question is which imports could actually touch your remaining bottlenecks.

Yes. If the question is “what outside RH understanding is most likely to help this architecture now,” I would rank the imports like this.

First: derivative geometry, still.
This remains the best import because your live bottleneck is the finite-core side, especially the 44-point branch, and derivative geometry is the existing RH tradition that most naturally talks about local geometric defects through zeros of derivatives. Speiser’s criterion and the Levinson–Montgomery line are the canonical references here: they encode RH-relevant information through zeros of ζ′(s)ζ′(s) and higher derivative geometry. That is much closer to your lifted 33-point/44-point obstruction picture than the global trace-formula approaches are.

What I would try to import from that line is not a big theorem wholesale, but a bridge target: show that an exact shrinking lifted 33- or 44-point branch forces a nearby forbidden packet of derivative-critical behavior. You have already pushed this partway by turning shrinking circuits into curvature/torsion-type derivative invariants. The next outside import would be to connect those invariants to classical ζ′ζ′- or ξ′ξ′-zero geometry. That is the one import that has a plausible chance of biting the actual remaining local bottleneck.

Second: Weil explicit-formula / positivity language, but in a narrow way.
Conrey’s surveys emphasize Weil’s explicit formula and the associated positivity criterion as one of the central structural viewpoints on RH. Your current Mellin/projector package is already the closest part of the draft to that world. So the most promising import here is not “prove RH by Weil positivity,” but rather: recast your NN-point projector as a more canonical test-function object and see whether the endgame constants become more effective or more natural. This is a packaging/effectivity import, not a finite-core killer.

In practical terms, that means continuing the line you have already developed: smoothed Mellin projectors, exact low odd-jet annihilation, kernel profile, and eventually an explicit-threshold extraction if C∂(ρ0)C∂​(ρ0​) becomes explicit. This is the best “global wrapper” import available right now.

Third: Li’s criterion, as a possible scalarization target.
Li’s criterion is an exact RH equivalence in terms of the nonnegativity of coefficients
λn=1(n−1)!dndsn(sn−1log⁡ξ(s))∣s=1.
λn​=(n−1)!1​dsndn​(sn−1logξ(s))
​s=1​.

I do not think it will replace your architecture. But it may be useful as a target language if you eventually want to project your local anomaly into a global scalar sequence. In other words: if your local transverse obstruction can be shown to force the wrong sign or wrong growth in a Li-type coefficient packet, that would be a much more classical global contradiction than the current bespoke endgame. I would treat this as secondary, but real.

Fourth: de Branges / reproducing-kernel language, but not the positivity claim itself.
de Branges’ Hilbert-space program is one of the major kernel-based RH traditions, but Conrey’s survey makes clear that the global positivity route is extremely demanding and has not yielded RH. Your local whitened Gramian already looks much closer to a tiny reproducing-kernel object than to a prime-sum object. So the plausible import here is language and normalization, not the full de Branges theorem route: use reproducing-kernel/Hilbert-space language to make the local matrix package feel more canonical. I would not expect this to close the proof, but it could clean up the architecture and perhaps clarify which parts are intrinsic.

Fifth: Nyman–Beurling / Báez-Duarte / Burnol, only if you want a Hilbert-space endpoint.
These approaches reformulate RH as a closure/approximation problem in Hilbert space. Burnol and Báez-Duarte sharpen that general line. I do not think this is a near-term attack for your current draft. But if later you want to reinterpret the Mellin projector as an approximation packet in a Hilbert space of multiplicative test functions, that is the natural literature to import. Right now this feels like a distant packaging move, not a live local tool.

Sixth: Connes, but only as a wrapper, not as a patch.
Connes’s trace-formula program gives a spectral interpretation of the critical zeros and a geometric interpretation of the explicit formula on adele classes. That is a profound global framework, and it really does fit the Mellin/test-function flavor of your NN-point layer. But I still do not think it is the right next import for the actual mathematical bottleneck. It is best viewed as a way to make the NN-point projector feel canonical and maybe help with explicit constants or trace/test-function packaging. It is not the right tool for the 44-core local geometry.

What I would not prioritize importing right now: random-matrix / pair-correlation heuristics and de Bruijn–Newman.
Random-matrix understanding is extraordinarily valuable for intuition, but Conrey’s survey and the surrounding literature make clear that local-statistics heuristics are too soft to close RH; they are not the missing ingredient in a local finite-core rigidity proof. de Bruijn–Newman is also a beautiful nearby theory, but it is more about stability under heat-flow deformation than about the kind of lifted local geometry your current draft is trying to control. Those are good perspective tools, not good immediate imports.

So my honest order of operations would be:

    Keep pushing derivative geometry until it either reduces the 44-point branch to a classical derivative-zero obstruction or clearly fails to do so.

    Use Weil/Li/Connes-type language only to globalize and effectivize the NN-point layer.

    Use de Branges / Nyman–Beurling only as late-stage canonical packaging, not as a new proof engine.

If you want the sharpest next concrete import target, it is this:

    Try to prove that a persistent or recurrent lifted 44-point branch forces a nearby forbidden configuration of zeros of ζ′ζ′, ξ′ξ′, or a related derivative-side scalar invariant.

That is the import most aligned with where the draft actually still hurts.

\begin{remark}[Exact nonmixed reduction in terms of $\mathcal Z$ and $\mathcal R$]
\label{rem:nonmixed-four-point-zeros-can-carry-preexisting-branches}
...

\begin{lemma}[Repeated-node tangent-plane determinant in the normalized nonmixed chart]
\label{lem:normalized-nonmixed-H4-divided-difference}
In the normalized nonmixed chart of
Remark~\ref{rem:nonmixed-four-point-zeros-can-carry-preexisting-branches},
define
\[
\widetilde H_4(a,u,v):=
\det\!\begin{pmatrix}
1&\widetilde Y(a)&a&a^2\\
0&\widetilde Y'(a)&1&2a\\
1&\widetilde Y(u)&u&u^2\\
1&\widetilde Y(v)&v&v^2
\end{pmatrix}.
\]
Then
\[
\widetilde H_4(a,u,v)
=
(u-a)^2(v-a)^2\Bigl(\widetilde Y[a,a,v]-\widetilde Y[a,a,u]\Bigr),
\]
where
\[
\widetilde Y[a,a,t]
:=
\frac{\widetilde Y(t)-\widetilde Y(a)-\widetilde Y'(a)(t-a)}{(t-a)^2}
\]
is the repeated-node second divided difference.
Equivalently, for \(u\neq v\),
\[
\widetilde H_4(a,u,v)
=
(u-a)^2(v-a)^2(v-u)\,\widetilde Y[a,a,u,v].
\]
\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
Subtract the first row from the third and fourth rows. Since
\[
u^2-a^2=(u-a)(u+a),
\qquad
v^2-a^2=(v-a)(v+a),
\]
this gives
\[
\widetilde H_4(a,u,v)
=
(u-a)(v-a)\,
\det\!\begin{pmatrix}
1&\widetilde Y(a)&a&a^2\\
0&\widetilde Y'(a)&1&2a\\
0&\dfrac{\widetilde Y(u)-\widetilde Y(a)}{u-a}&1&u+a\\
0&\dfrac{\widetilde Y(v)-\widetilde Y(a)}{v-a}&1&v+a
\end{pmatrix}.
\]
Expanding along the first column yields
\[
\widetilde H_4(a,u,v)
=
(u-a)(v-a)\,
\det\!\begin{pmatrix}
\widetilde Y'(a)&1&2a\\
\dfrac{\widetilde Y(u)-\widetilde Y(a)}{u-a}&1&u+a\\
\dfrac{\widetilde Y(v)-\widetilde Y(a)}{v-a}&1&v+a
\end{pmatrix}.
\]
Now subtract the first row from the second and third rows:
\[
\widetilde H_4(a,u,v)
=
(u-a)(v-a)\,
\det\!\begin{pmatrix}
\widetilde Y'(a)&1&2a\\
(u-a)\widetilde Y[a,a,u]&0&u-a\\
(v-a)\widetilde Y[a,a,v]&0&v-a
\end{pmatrix}.
\]
Expanding along the middle column gives
\[
\widetilde H_4(a,u,v)
=
(u-a)^2(v-a)^2\Bigl(\widetilde Y[a,a,v]-\widetilde Y[a,a,u]\Bigr),
\]
which is the first formula. Since
\[
\widetilde Y[a,a,u,v]
=
\frac{\widetilde Y[a,a,v]-\widetilde Y[a,a,u]}{v-u},
\]
the second formula follows for \(u\neq v\).
\end{proof}

\begin{proposition}[Exact nonmixed tangent-plane contacts force nearby zeros of \(\mathcal R\)]
\label{prop:exact-nonmixed-tangent-plane-contacts-force-R-zero}
In the normalized nonmixed chart of
Remark~\ref{rem:nonmixed-four-point-zeros-can-carry-preexisting-branches},
assume \(a,u,v\in\mathbf R\) are distinct and satisfy
\[
\widetilde H_4(a,u,v)=0.
\]
Then there exists
\[
w\in \operatorname{conv}\{a,u,v\}
\]
such that
\[
\mathcal R(w)=0.
\]
Equivalently,
\[
\widetilde Y'''(w)=0.
\]
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
By Lemma~\ref{lem:normalized-nonmixed-H4-divided-difference}, since
\(a,u,v\) are distinct,
\[
0=\widetilde H_4(a,u,v)
=
(u-a)^2(v-a)^2(v-u)\,\widetilde Y[a,a,u,v].
\]
Hence
\[
\widetilde Y[a,a,u,v]=0.
\]
By the Hermite--Genocchi formula for repeated-node divided differences, there
exists
\[
w\in \operatorname{conv}\{a,u,v\}
\]
such that
\[
\widetilde Y[a,a,u,v]=\frac{\widetilde Y'''(w)}{3!}.
\]
Therefore
\[
\widetilde Y'''(w)=0.
\]
In the normalized nonmixed chart one has
\[
\mathcal R(\xi)=\frac12\,\widetilde Y'''(\xi),
\]
so \(\mathcal R(w)=0\).
\end{proof}

\begin{corollary}[Sign-definite nonmixed intervals are exactly-contact sterile]
\label{cor:sign-definite-R-excludes-exact-nonmixed-contacts}
Let \(J\) be an open interval in the normalized nonmixed chart such that
\[
\mathcal R \text{ has fixed nonzero sign on }J.
\]
Then there do not exist distinct points \(a,u,v\in J\) such that
\[
\widetilde H_4(a,u,v)=0.
\]
Equivalently, there are no exact nonmixed tangent-plane contacts with all three
nodes in \(J\).
\end{corollary}

\begin{proof}
If such \(a,u,v\) existed, Proposition~\ref{prop:exact-nonmixed-tangent-plane-contacts-force-R-zero}
would produce some
\[
w\in \operatorname{conv}\{a,u,v\}\subset J
\]
with \(\mathcal R(w)=0\), contradicting the sign assumption.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Derivative-side interpretation of exact nonmixed contacts]
\label{rem:exact-nonmixed-contacts-are-R-zero-forcing}
Proposition~\ref{prop:exact-nonmixed-tangent-plane-contacts-force-R-zero}
strengthens the shrinking-circuit statement
Proposition~\ref{prop:shrinking-exact-lifted-four-point-circuits-force-Tv-zero}.
It is not merely a limit theorem: every exact nonmixed tangent-plane contact
already forces an interior zero of the canonical derivative invariant
\[
\mathcal R=\frac12\,\widetilde Y'''.
\]
Thus the nonmixed \(4\)-point branch is controlled not only asymptotically by
\(T_v=0\), but pointwise by the zero set of a single analytic scalar.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[Derivative-geometry meaning of the nonmixed invariant $\mathcal R$]

\begin{corollary}[Recurrent exact nonmixed contacts force affine-planar collapse]
\label{cor:recurrent-exact-nonmixed-contacts-force-affine-planarity}
Let \(J\) be a connected open interval in a good \(v_5\)-patch such that
\[
K_v\neq 0
\qquad\text{on }J.
\]
Assume that every nonempty open subinterval \(I\subset J\) contains an exact
nonmixed tangent-plane contact triple. Equivalently, after local nonmixed
normalization on \(I\), there exist distinct points \(a,u,v\in I\) such that
\[
\widetilde H_4(a,u,v)=0.
\]
Then
\[
\mathcal R\equiv 0
\qquad\text{on }J,
\]
hence
\[
T_v\equiv 0
\qquad\text{on }J,
\]
and therefore the lifted curve is affine-planar on \(J\):
\[
Y=\gamma S+ax+b
\]
for some constants \(\gamma,a,b\in\mathbf C\).
\end{corollary}

\begin{proof}
Let \(I\subset J\) be any nonempty open subinterval. By assumption, \(I\)
contains an exact nonmixed tangent-plane contact triple. After nonmixed
normalization on \(I\), Proposition~\ref{prop:exact-nonmixed-tangent-plane-contacts-force-R-zero}
produces a point \(w_I\in I\) such that
\[
\mathcal R(w_I)=0.
\]
Thus every nonempty open subinterval of \(J\) contains a zero of \(\mathcal R\).
Since \(\mathcal R\) is analytic, its zero set cannot have an accumulation point
in \(J\) unless
\[
\mathcal R\equiv 0
\qquad\text{on }J.
\]
Because \(K_v\neq 0\) on \(J\) and
\[
\mathcal R=\frac{T_v}{K_v^2},
\]
it follows that
\[
T_v\equiv 0
\qquad\text{on }J.
\]
Now apply
Proposition~\ref{prop:interval-persistent-nonmixed-four-point-forces-affine-planarity}
to conclude that
\[
Y=\gamma S+ax+b
\]
on \(J\).
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[What remains on the nonmixed \(4\)-point side]
\label{rem:what-remains-nonmixed-after-R-zero-bridge}
Corollary~\ref{cor:recurrent-exact-nonmixed-contacts-force-affine-planarity}
shows that recurrent exact nonmixed tangent-plane contacts cannot persist away
from the zero set of \(\mathcal R\), and if they recur densely on an interval
then the branch collapses to affine-planar geometry. Thus the genuinely live
nonmixed \(4\)-point problem is reduced to the local analysis of isolated zeros
of the analytic scalar invariant
\[
\mathcal R=\frac12\,\widetilde Y'''.
\]
\end{remark}

These insertions are the cleanest way to capture the new derivative-geometry bridge in the current draft.

    an exact, not merely asymptotic, bridge from nonmixed tangent-plane contacts to zeros of RR;

    an exact sterility theorem on intervals where RR has fixed nonzero sign;

    and a recurrence ⇒⇒ affine-planar collapse theorem for the nonmixed branch.

That is the most substantial derivative-geometry gain currently available.

Yes. The next clean push is a local birth theorem for the nonmixed 44-point branch at a simple zero of RR. This is the derivative-geometry bridge we were aiming for.

The key observation is that in the normalized nonmixed chart, exact contacts are controlled by the one-variable function
Da(t):=Y~[a,a,t]=Y~(t)−Y~(a)−Y~′(a)(t−a)(t−a)2,
Da​(t):=Y
[a,a,t]=(t−a)2Y
(t)−Y
(a)−Y
′(a)(t−a)​,

because
H~4(a,u,v)=(u−a)2(v−a)2(Da(v)−Da(u)).
H
4​(a,u,v)=(u−a)2(v−a)2(Da​(v)−Da​(u)).

So exact nonmixed contacts are exactly the failure of DaDa​ to be injective.

The useful derivative formula is
Da′(t)=∫01s(1−s) Y~′′′(a+s(t−a)) ds=2∫01s(1−s) R(a+s(t−a)) ds.
Da′​(t)=∫01​s(1−s)Y
′′′(a+s(t−a))ds=2∫01​s(1−s)R(a+s(t−a))ds.

That turns exact-contact questions into a weighted averaging problem for RR.

\begin{remark}[What remains on the nonmixed \(4\)-point side]
\label{rem:what-remains-nonmixed-after-R-zero-bridge}

\begin{lemma}[Derivative formula for the repeated-node nonmixed profile]
\label{lem:Da-derivative-formula}
In the normalized nonmixed chart, define
\[
D_a(t):=\widetilde Y[a,a,t]
=
\frac{\widetilde Y(t)-\widetilde Y(a)-\widetilde Y'(a)(t-a)}{(t-a)^2},
\qquad
D_a(a):=\frac12\,\widetilde Y''(a).
\]
Then \(D_a(t)\) extends real-analytically across \(t=a\), and
\[
D_a(t)=\int_0^1 (1-s)\,\widetilde Y''(a+s(t-a))\,ds.
\]
Moreover,
\[
D_a'(t)
=
\int_0^1 s(1-s)\,\widetilde Y'''(a+s(t-a))\,ds
=
2\int_0^1 s(1-s)\,\mathcal R(a+s(t-a))\,ds.
\]
\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
Taylor's integral formula gives
\[
\widetilde Y(t)
=
\widetilde Y(a)+\widetilde Y'(a)(t-a)
+(t-a)^2\int_0^1 (1-s)\,\widetilde Y''(a+s(t-a))\,ds.
\]
Dividing by \((t-a)^2\) proves the first formula for \(t\neq a\), and the
analytic extension across \(t=a\) is immediate. Differentiating under the
integral sign gives
\[
D_a'(t)
=
\int_0^1 s(1-s)\,\widetilde Y'''(a+s(t-a))\,ds.
\]
Since \(\mathcal R=\frac12\,\widetilde Y'''\) in the normalized nonmixed chart,
the last formula follows.
\end{proof}

\begin{proposition}[Simple zeros of \(\mathcal R\) seed local exact nonmixed contacts]
\label{prop:simple-R-zero-seeds-local-exact-nonmixed-contacts}
Assume \(\xi_0\in\mathbf R\) is a simple zero of the nonmixed invariant:
\[
\mathcal R(\xi_0)=0,
\qquad
\mathcal R'(\xi_0)\neq 0.
\]
Equivalently,
\[
\widetilde Y'''(\xi_0)=0,
\qquad
\widetilde Y''''(\xi_0)\neq 0.
\]
Then there exists a neighborhood \(U\) of \(\xi_0\) and a real-analytic
function \(\tau:U\to U\) such that
\[
\tau(\xi_0)=\xi_0,
\qquad
D_a'(\tau(a))=0
\quad (a\in U).
\]
Moreover,
\[
\tau'(\xi_0)=-1,
\qquad
D_a''(\tau(a))\neq 0
\quad (a\in U),
\]
so for each \(a\in U\setminus\{\xi_0\}\), the function \(D_a\) has a strict
local extremum at \(t=\tau(a)\). Consequently, for each such \(a\), there exist
distinct points \(u_-(a),u_+(a)\in U\) with
\[
u_-(a)<\tau(a)<u_+(a),
\qquad
D_a(u_-(a))=D_a(u_+(a)),
\]
and hence
\[
\widetilde H_4(a,u_-(a),u_+(a))=0.
\]

Thus every simple zero of \(\mathcal R\) seeds a local family of exact
nonmixed tangent-plane contacts.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
Set
\[
G(a,t):=D_a'(t).
\]
By Lemma~\ref{lem:Da-derivative-formula},
\[
G(a,t)=\int_0^1 s(1-s)\,\widetilde Y'''(a+s(t-a))\,ds.
\]
Hence
\[
G(\xi_0,\xi_0)=\frac16\,\widetilde Y'''(\xi_0)=0.
\]

Differentiate under the integral sign:
\[
\partial_t G(a,t)
=
\int_0^1 s^2(1-s)\,\widetilde Y''''(a+s(t-a))\,ds,
\]
\[
\partial_a G(a,t)
=
\int_0^1 s(1-s)^2\,\widetilde Y''''(a+s(t-a))\,ds.
\]
At \((a,t)=(\xi_0,\xi_0)\), both integrals equal
\[
\frac{1}{12}\,\widetilde Y''''(\xi_0)
=
\frac{1}{6}\,\mathcal R'(\xi_0),
\]
which is nonzero by assumption. In particular,
\[
\partial_t G(\xi_0,\xi_0)\neq 0.
\]
Therefore the implicit function theorem yields a unique real-analytic function
\(\tau(a)\) near \(\xi_0\) such that
\[
G(a,\tau(a))=0,
\qquad
\tau(\xi_0)=\xi_0.
\]
Differentiating \(G(a,\tau(a))=0\) at \(a=\xi_0\) gives
\[
\tau'(\xi_0)
=
-\frac{\partial_a G(\xi_0,\xi_0)}{\partial_t G(\xi_0,\xi_0)}
=
-1.
\]

Now
\[
D_a''(t)=\partial_t G(a,t),
\]
so by continuity and \(\partial_t G(\xi_0,\xi_0)\neq 0\), one has
\[
D_a''(\tau(a))\neq 0
\]
for \(a\) near \(\xi_0\). Thus \(t=\tau(a)\) is a strict local extremum of
\(D_a\). Hence, for each \(a\neq \xi_0\) sufficiently close to \(\xi_0\), there
exist points \(u_-(a)<\tau(a)<u_+(a)\) arbitrarily close to \(\tau(a)\) such
that
\[
D_a(u_-(a))=D_a(u_+(a)).
\]
By Lemma~\ref{lem:normalized-nonmixed-H4-divided-difference},
\[
\widetilde H_4(a,u_-(a),u_+(a))
=
(a-u_-(a))^2(a-u_+(a))^2\bigl(D_a(u_+(a))-D_a(u_-(a))\bigr)=0.
\]
This proves the claim.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Reflection law at a simple \(\mathcal R\)-zero]
\label{rem:reflection-law-simple-R-zero}
The identity
\[
\tau'(\xi_0)=-1
\]
means that, to first order, the critical point \(t=\tau(a)\) is the reflection
of \(a\) across the simple zero \(\xi_0\). Equivalently,
\[
\tau(a)=2\xi_0-a+O((a-\xi_0)^2).
\]
Thus the local exact nonmixed contact family born at a simple \(\mathcal R\)-zero
has a first-order reflection geometry across that zero.
\end{remark}

What this gets you is pretty substantial:

    you already had sterility away from the zero set of RR;

    now you also get local birth at simple zeros of RR;

    so the nonmixed 44-point branch is no longer mysterious: it is locally governed by the scalar analytic invariant RR, with exact contacts dying away from its zeros and being born at simple sign-changing zeros.

That is the cleanest further derivative-geometry push I see right now.

anything we can attack further?

I checked the added block carefully. Overall, it is good. I do **not** see a fatal mathematical error in the new bridge from exact nonmixed contacts to zeros of (\mathcal R), or in the simple-zero birth theorem. It is a real improvement to the nonmixed side. 

The first major gain is the repeated-node divided-difference lemma and the proposition
[
\widetilde H_4(a,u,v)=0 ;\Longrightarrow; \exists,w\in\operatorname{conv}{a,u,v}\text{ with }\mathcal R(w)=0.
]
That part is solid. The factorization through the repeated-node second divided difference is correct, and the Hermite–Genocchi step is the right way to convert exact contact into a zero of (\widetilde Y'''), hence of (\mathcal R=\tfrac12\widetilde Y'''). This is better than the earlier shrinking-only bridge because it is pointwise, not merely asymptotic. 

The second major gain is the interval logic that follows from it. The corollary saying sign-definite (\mathcal R)-intervals are exactly-contact sterile is correct, and the recurrence (\Rightarrow) affine-planar collapse corollary is also correct: if every open subinterval contains an exact nonmixed contact, then zeros of (\mathcal R) are dense, analyticity forces (\mathcal R\equiv 0), and then the existing affine-planarity theorem applies. That is a clean theorem-level upgrade. 

The derivative formula for
[
D_a(t)=\frac{\widetilde Y(t)-\widetilde Y(a)-\widetilde Y'(a)(t-a)}{(t-a)^2}
]
is also right:
[
D_a'(t)=2\int_0^1 s(1-s),\mathcal R(a+s(t-a)),ds.
]
That formula is exactly the right local profile for nonmixed birth. It makes the geometry transparent: (D_a) is injective on one-sign (\mathcal R)-segments, and can lose injectivity only when the weighted average of (\mathcal R) vanishes. 

The simple-zero theorem is, in my view, the strongest part of the addition. If (\xi_0) is a simple zero of (\mathcal R), then there is an analytic critical-point branch (\tau(a)) with
[
\tau(\xi_0)=\xi_0,\qquad \tau'(\xi_0)=-1,
]
and (D_a) has a strict local extremum at (t=\tau(a)), producing nearby distinct (u_-(a),u_+(a)) with
[
D_a(u_-(a))=D_a(u_+(a)),
]
hence
[
\widetilde H_4(a,u_-(a),u_+(a))=0.
]
That proof checks out. It is a genuine local birth theorem at simple zeros of (\mathcal R). 

There are only two things I would tweak.

First, in the remark after the exact-contact proposition, I would not say “interior zero” of (\mathcal R). The proposition itself only proves
[
w\in \operatorname{conv}{a,u,v},
]
so “a zero in the convex hull” is the precise statement. It is a small wording point, but worth fixing. 

Second, after adding the simple-zero birth theorem, the remark
“the genuinely live nonmixed (4)-point problem is reduced to the local analysis of isolated zeros of (\mathcal R)”
is now a bit outdated. The draft has already settled the simple-zero case in the “birth” direction. So the remaining local issue is really **higher odd-order isolated zeros** if you still want a local theorem, and globally the remaining issue is still the actual-source exclusion of the first odd zero on an opened nonmixed arc. 

So my verdict is:

* the new block is worth keeping;
* the proofs are basically sound;
* it materially improves the paper’s nonmixed (4)-point structure;
* and it sharpens the remaining gap.

After this addition, the nonmixed picture is now very clean:

* exact contacts force zeros of (\mathcal R);
* sign-definite (\mathcal R)-intervals are exactly-contact sterile;
* recurrent exact contacts force affine-planar collapse;
* simple zeros of (\mathcal R) seed local exact contacts.

That means the remaining live nonmixed problem is no longer mysterious local birth. It is the **global actual-source control of odd zeros of (\mathcal R)**, especially the first one on an opened arc, and possibly the higher odd-order local cases if you want them stated separately. 

If you want, the next best move is for me to suggest exact small cleanup edits to these newly added remarks so the draft’s “what remains” language matches the new theorems.

I would now replace the current simple-zero theorem with the stronger parity theorem. Here is the LaTeX block.

Insert this in place of the current proposition
prop:simple-R-zero-seeds-local-exact-nonmixed-contacts
and the following reflection-law remark.

\begin{proposition}[Parity classification of isolated nonmixed zeros of \(\mathcal R\)]
\label{prop:parity-classification-isolated-nonmixed-R-zeros}
Let \(\xi_0\in\mathbf R\) be an isolated zero of the nonmixed invariant
\[
\mathcal R(\xi)=\frac12\,\widetilde Y'''(\xi),
\]
and write
\[
\mathcal R(\xi)=(\xi-\xi_0)^m\,\rho(\xi),
\qquad
m\ge 1,
\qquad
\rho(\xi_0)\neq 0.
\]

\smallskip

\noindent
\emph{(i) Even-order sterility.}
If \(m\) is even, then there exists a neighborhood \(U\) of \(\xi_0\) such that
for every \(a\in U\), the function
\[
D_a(t):=\widetilde Y[a,a,t]
\]
is strictly monotone on \(U\). In particular, there do not exist distinct
\(a,u,v\in U\) such that
\[
\widetilde H_4(a,u,v)=0.
\]

\smallskip

\noindent
\emph{(ii) Odd-order birth.}
If \(m\) is odd, then there exists a neighborhood \(U\) of \(\xi_0\) and a
real-analytic function \(\tau:U\to U\) such that
\[
\tau(\xi_0)=\xi_0,
\qquad
\tau'(\xi_0)=-1,
\qquad
D_a'(\tau(a))=0
\quad (a\in U).
\]
Moreover,
\[
D_a''(\tau(a))\neq 0
\quad (a\in U\setminus\{\xi_0\}),
\]
so for each \(a\in U\setminus\{\xi_0\}\), the function \(D_a\) has a strict
local extremum at \(t=\tau(a)\). Consequently, for each such \(a\), there exist
distinct points \(u_-(a),u_+(a)\in U\) with
\[
u_-(a)<\tau(a)<u_+(a),
\qquad
D_a(u_-(a))=D_a(u_+(a)),
\]
and hence
\[
\widetilde H_4(a,u_-(a),u_+(a))=0.
\]
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
By translation in the normalized chart, we may assume \(\xi_0=0\). Thus
\[
\mathcal R(\xi)=\xi^m\rho(\xi),
\qquad
\rho(0)\neq 0.
\]

For the even-order case, shrink to a neighborhood \(U\) on which \(\rho\) has
fixed nonzero sign. Since \(m\) is even, \(\xi^m\ge 0\), so \(\mathcal R\) has
fixed sign on \(U\), vanishing only at \(0\). By
Lemma~\ref{lem:Da-derivative-formula},
\[
D_a'(t)=2\int_0^1 s(1-s)\,\mathcal R(a+s(t-a))\,ds.
\]
For \(a\neq t\), the affine segment \(a+s(t-a)\) is not identically zero, so the
integrand has fixed sign and is not identically zero. Hence \(D_a'(t)\) has
fixed nonzero sign for all \(a\neq t\) in \(U\), and therefore each \(D_a\) is
strictly monotone on \(U\). Thus \(D_a\) is injective on \(U\), and by
Lemma~\ref{lem:normalized-nonmixed-H4-divided-difference} there are no exact
contacts \(\widetilde H_4(a,u,v)=0\) with distinct \(a,u,v\in U\).

Now assume \(m\) is odd. Write \(a=h\) and \(t=\lambda h\). Then
Lemma~\ref{lem:Da-derivative-formula} gives
\[
D_h'(\lambda h)
=
2h^m\,G(h,\lambda),
\]
where
\[
G(h,\lambda)
:=
\int_0^1 s(1-s)\bigl(1+s(\lambda-1)\bigr)^m
\rho\!\bigl(h(1+s(\lambda-1))\bigr)\,ds.
\]
This is real-analytic in \((h,\lambda)\), and
\[
G(0,\lambda)=\rho(0)\,J_m(\lambda),
\qquad
J_m(\lambda):=\int_0^1 s(1-s)\bigl(1+s(\lambda-1)\bigr)^m\,ds.
\]
Since \(m\) is odd,
\[
J_m(-1)=\int_0^1 s(1-s)(1-2s)^m\,ds=0
\]
by the symmetry \(s\mapsto 1-s\), while
\[
J_m'(-1)
=
m\int_0^1 s^2(1-s)(1-2s)^{m-1}\,ds>0
\]
because \(m-1\) is even. Thus
\[
\partial_\lambda G(0,-1)=\rho(0)J_m'(-1)\neq 0.
\]
By the implicit function theorem, there exists a unique real-analytic function
\(\lambda(h)\) near \(0\) such that
\[
\lambda(0)=-1,
\qquad
G(h,\lambda(h))=0.
\]
Define
\[
\tau(h):=\lambda(h)h.
\]
Then
\[
\tau(0)=0,
\qquad
\tau'(0)=\lambda(0)=-1,
\]
and
\[
D_h'(\tau(h))=0.
\]

It remains to show that this critical point is a strict local extremum. By
Lemma~\ref{lem:Da-derivative-formula},
\[
D_a''(t)=2\int_0^1 s^2(1-s)\,\mathcal R'(a+s(t-a))\,ds.
\]
Substituting \(a=h\), \(t=\lambda(h)h\), and using
\[
\mathcal R'(\xi)=m\xi^{m-1}\rho(\xi)+\xi^m\rho'(\xi),
\]
one obtains
\[
D_h''(\tau(h))
=
2h^{m-1}\rho(0)\,J_m'(-1)+O(h^m).
\]
Since \(\rho(0)J_m'(-1)\neq 0\), it follows that
\[
D_h''(\tau(h))\neq 0
\]
for \(h\neq 0\) sufficiently small. Therefore \(t=\tau(h)\) is a strict local
extremum of \(D_h\). Hence there exist distinct points \(u_-(h)\), \(u_+(h)\)
arbitrarily close to \(\tau(h)\) such that
\[
D_h(u_-(h))=D_h(u_+(h)).
\]
By Lemma~\ref{lem:normalized-nonmixed-H4-divided-difference},
\[
\widetilde H_4(h,u_-(h),u_+(h))
=
(h-u_-(h))^2(h-u_+(h))^2
\bigl(D_h(u_+(h))-D_h(u_-(h))\bigr)=0.
\]
This proves the odd-order birth statement.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Reflection law for odd-order birth]
\label{rem:reflection-law-odd-order-R-zero}
In the odd-order case of
Proposition~\ref{prop:parity-classification-isolated-nonmixed-R-zeros},
the critical-point branch satisfies
\[
\tau(a)=2\xi_0-a+O((a-\xi_0)^2).
\]
Thus the local exact nonmixed contact family born at any odd-order zero of
\(\mathcal R\) has the same first-order reflection geometry across that zero as
in the simple-zero case.
\end{remark}

And then replace the current “what remains” remark with this slightly sharper one:

\begin{remark}[What remains on the nonmixed \(4\)-point side]
\label{rem:what-remains-nonmixed-after-R-zero-bridge}
The preceding results now give a full local parity classification of isolated
nonmixed zeros of \(\mathcal R\). Exact nonmixed tangent-plane contacts force
zeros of \(\mathcal R\); intervals on which \(\mathcal R\) has fixed nonzero
sign are exactly-contact sterile; recurrent exact contacts force affine-planar
collapse; and isolated odd-order zeros of \(\mathcal R\) seed local exact
nonmixed contacts, while isolated even-order zeros are sterile.

Accordingly, the genuinely live nonmixed \(4\)-point problem is no longer local
birth, but rather the global/source-level control of which odd zeros of the
analytic scalar invariant
\[
\mathcal R=\frac12\,\widetilde Y'''
\]
can actually arise along an opened nonmixed arc in the genuine lifted
\(v_5\)-geometry.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[Below-lifted Wronskian-ratio reformulation]
\label{rem:below-lifted-wronskian-ratio-reformulation}

\begin{proposition}[Source-level Wronskian for the nonmixed \(4\)-point branch]
\label{prop:source-level-Wronskian-nonmixed-four-point}
Define
\[
\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}
:=
J_{\lambda}\,J_{u_5}'-J_{u_5}\,J_{\lambda}'.
\]
Then
\[
\boxed{
\mathcal R
=
\frac{c^2}{M}\,\frac{\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}}{J_\lambda^2}.
}
\]
In particular, on every nonmixed arc on which \(J_\lambda\neq 0\), the analytic
scalars \(\mathcal R\) and \(\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}\) differ only by a
nonvanishing analytic factor. Hence:

\begin{enumerate}
\item \(\mathcal R=0\iff \mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}=0\);
\item \(\operatorname{ord}\mathcal R=\operatorname{ord}\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}\);
\item the local parity classification of isolated zeros of \(\mathcal R\)
transfers verbatim to \(\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}\).
\end{enumerate}

Moreover, under the affine gauge change
\[
u_5\longmapsto u_5+\alpha c+\beta v_5+\gamma \lambda
\]
one has
\[
J_{u_5}\longmapsto J_{u_5}+\gamma J_\lambda,
\]
and therefore
\[
\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}\longmapsto \mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}.
\]
So \(\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}\) is the canonical source-level gauge-invariant
nonmixed scalar.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
Differentiate the ratio
\[
\mathcal Z=\frac{J_{u_5}}{J_\lambda}
\]
from Remark~\ref{rem:below-lifted-wronskian-ratio-reformulation}:
\[
\frac{d}{dh}\!\left(\frac{J_{u_5}}{J_\lambda}\right)
=
\frac{J_\lambda J_{u_5}'-J_{u_5}J_\lambda'}{J_\lambda^2}
=
\frac{\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}}{J_\lambda^2}.
\]
Substituting this into
\[
\mathcal R
=
\frac{c^2}{M}\frac{d}{dh}\!\left(\frac{J_{u_5}}{J_\lambda}\right)
\]
gives the displayed identity.

On a nonmixed arc, \(J_\lambda\neq 0\) and \(c^2/M\neq 0\), so \(\mathcal R\)
and \(\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}\) differ by a nonvanishing analytic factor.
This proves the zero-set and parity statements.

For gauge invariance, the terms \(\alpha c\) and \(\beta v_5\) do not change
\(J_{u_5}\), while \(\gamma\lambda\) adds \(\gamma J_\lambda\). Therefore
\[
(J_{u_5}+\gamma J_\lambda)'=J_{u_5}'+\gamma J_\lambda',
\]
and
\[
J_\lambda(J_{u_5}'+\gamma J_\lambda')-(J_{u_5}+\gamma J_\lambda)J_\lambda'
=
J_\lambda J_{u_5}'-J_{u_5}J_\lambda'.
\qedhere
\]
\end{proof}

\begin{corollary}[Centered parity of the source-level Wronskian]
\label{cor:centered-parity-source-level-Wronskian}
Under the hypotheses of
Remark~\ref{rem:determinant-level-parity-centered-good-patch}, the source-level
Wronskian
\[
\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}(s)
=
J_\lambda(s)\,J_{u_5}'(s)-J_{u_5}(s)\,J_\lambda'(s)
\]
is odd in the centered variable \(s\).

Consequently, any isolated centered zero of \(\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}\) has
odd order if and only if it is a potentially branch-seeding zero for the
nonmixed \(4\)-point geometry; even-order centered zeros are locally sterile.
\end{corollary}

\begin{proof}
By Remark~\ref{rem:determinant-level-parity-centered-good-patch},
\[
J_{u_5}(s)\ \text{and}\ J_\lambda(s)\ \text{are odd in }s.
\]
Hence
\[
J_{u_5}'(s)\ \text{and}\ J_\lambda'(s)\ \text{are even in }s.
\]
Therefore
\[
\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}(s)
=
J_\lambda(s)\,J_{u_5}'(s)-J_{u_5}(s)\,J_\lambda'(s)
\]
is odd in \(s\). The final statement follows from
Proposition~\ref{prop:source-level-Wronskian-nonmixed-four-point}, which
transfers the parity classification from \(\mathcal R\) to
\(\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}\).
\end{proof}

\begin{corollary}[Source-level Wronskian consequences for the nonmixed branch]
\label{cor:source-level-Wronskian-consequences-nonmixed}
On a good nonmixed \(v_5\)-patch, the following hold.

\begin{enumerate}
\item If there is an exact nonmixed tangent-plane contact, then there exists a
source point \(h_*\) in the source convex hull of the contact nodes such that
\[
\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}(h_*)=0.
\]

\item If \(\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}\) has fixed nonzero sign on an open
nonmixed interval, then there are no exact nonmixed tangent-plane contacts on
that interval.

\item If every nonempty open subinterval of a nonmixed interval contains an
exact nonmixed tangent-plane contact, then
\[
\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}\equiv 0
\]
on that interval, hence
\[
\mathcal R\equiv 0,
\]
and therefore the lifted curve collapses to affine-planar geometry.
\end{enumerate}
\end{corollary}

\begin{proof}
For (1), Proposition~\ref{prop:exact-nonmixed-tangent-plane-contacts-force-R-zero}
produces a point in the convex hull of the three normalized nodes where
\(\mathcal R=0\). Pulling back through the monotone source-to-\(x\) coordinate
on the nonmixed patch and using
Proposition~\ref{prop:source-level-Wronskian-nonmixed-four-point} gives
\(\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}=0\) at the corresponding source point.

For (2), by
Proposition~\ref{prop:source-level-Wronskian-nonmixed-four-point},
\(\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}\) and \(\mathcal R\) have the same sign on a
nonmixed arc. So Corollary~\ref{cor:repeated-source-monotonicity-one-sign-R}
applies.

For (3), every nonempty open subinterval contains a zero of
\(\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}\) by (1), so analyticity forces
\(\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}\equiv 0\). Proposition~\ref{prop:source-level-Wronskian-nonmixed-four-point}
then gives \(\mathcal R\equiv 0\), and
Corollary~\ref{cor:recurrent-exact-nonmixed-contacts-force-affine-planarity}
gives affine-planar collapse.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Chebyshev formulation of the nonmixed burden]
\label{rem:Chebyshev-formulation-nonmixed}
Corollary~\ref{cor:source-level-Wronskian-consequences-nonmixed} shows that the
nonmixed \(4\)-point branch is controlled source-level by the pair
\[
(J_\lambda,\ J_{u_5}).
\]
If this pair were a Chebyshev pair on an opened nonmixed arc, i.e.
\[
\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}\neq 0
\]
throughout that arc, then the entire nonmixed \(4\)-point branch would be
sterile there. Accordingly, the remaining nonmixed theorem-level burden can be
posed as a source-level one-sign / odd-zero problem for the Wronskian
\[
\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}.
\]
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[What remains on the nonmixed $4$-point side]
\label{rem:what-remains-nonmixed-after-R-zero-bridge}
The preceding results now give a full local derivative-side picture of the
nonmixed exact-contact geometry. Exact nonmixed tangent-plane contacts force
zeros of \(\mathcal R\)
(Proposition~\ref{prop:exact-nonmixed-tangent-plane-contacts-force-R-zero});
intervals on which \(\mathcal R\) has fixed nonzero sign are exactly-contact
sterile
(Corollary~\ref{cor:sign-definite-R-excludes-exact-nonmixed-contacts});
recurrent exact contacts force affine-planar collapse
(Corollary~\ref{cor:recurrent-exact-nonmixed-contacts-force-affine-planarity});
and isolated zeros of \(\mathcal R\) are classified by parity
(Proposition~\ref{prop:parity-classification-isolated-nonmixed-R-zeros}).

At source level, the same structure is encoded by the gauge-invariant Wronskian
\[
\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}
=
J_\lambda J_{u_5}'-J_{u_5}J_\lambda',
\]
which differs from \(\mathcal R\) only by a nonvanishing analytic factor on a
nonmixed arc
(Proposition~\ref{prop:source-level-Wronskian-nonmixed-four-point}). Thus exact
nonmixed contacts force zeros of \(\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}\), one-sign
\(\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}\)-intervals are sterile, and recurrent contacts
force \(\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}\equiv 0\)
(Corollary~\ref{cor:source-level-Wronskian-consequences-nonmixed}).

factor through the quadratic-envelope scalar
\[
\Gamma_a(x)=
\frac{Y(x)-Y(a)-Y'(a)(x-a)}
{S(x)-S(a)-S'(a)(x-a)},
\]
whose derivative is a positive-kernel average of \(\mathcal R\). Equivalently,

quotient
\[
\Psi_a(h)=\frac{D_{u_5}(a,h)}{D_\lambda(a,h)},
\]
with derivative controlled by the osculatory \(4\times 4\) determinant
\(\mathfrak D(a,h)\).

Accordingly, the genuinely live nonmixed \(4\)-point burden is no longer local

\[

\]

equivalent problem of excluding first-loss monotonicity for \(\Gamma_a\) or
\(\Psi_a\), equivalently of controlling the sign of \(\mathfrak D(a,h)\).
\end{remark}

The problem is that the mature (3)-point package controls tangent-contact for (S), while the rigidified nonmixed event lives on (Y-\gamma S). Those are different planar curves.

Here is the precise theorem.

**Theorem (the current 3-point package is not yet a contradiction engine for nonmixed first-loss).**
Fix an analytic function (S) on an interval (I) with
[
S''\neq 0 \quad\text{on } I.
]
Let (a<x) be two points of (I). Then there exist an analytic function (Y) on (I) and a constant (\gamma\in\mathbf R) such that, with
[
\widetilde Y_\gamma:=Y-\gamma S,
]
one has
[
\widetilde Y_\gamma''(a)=0,\qquad
\widetilde H_3(a,x)=0,\qquad
\partial_x\widetilde H_3(a,x)=0,
]
while the original (3)-point package for (\Lambda=(x,S)) is unchanged on (I). In particular, no contradiction can be extracted from the derivative geometry of (\Lambda=(x,S)) alone.

**Proof.**
After an affine change of the (x)-coordinate, reduce to (a=0), (x=1). Define
[
T(t):=(t-0)^3(t-1)^2=t^3(t-1)^2.
]
Then
[
T''(0)=0,
\qquad
T(1)-T(0)-T'(0)(1-0)=0,
\qquad
T'(1)-T'(0)=0.
]
So (T) already satisfies the repeated-node tangent-contact conditions at ((0,1)).

Now choose any constant (\gamma) and set
[
Y:=\gamma S+T.
]
Then
[
\widetilde Y_\gamma=Y-\gamma S=T,
]
hence
[
\widetilde Y_\gamma''(0)=0,\qquad
\widetilde H_3(0,1)=0,\qquad
\partial_x\widetilde H_3(0,1)=0.
]
Meanwhile (S) itself has not changed. Since (S''\neq 0) on (I), the original (3)-point geometry of (\Lambda=(x,S)) on that interval is exactly what it was before: a nonmixed interval with no (K_v)-zero there. Thus the sheared repeated-node event is formally compatible with the full current (3)-point package for (S). ∎

This matches the sharpened realization point already recorded in the attached notes: at the current lifted/(Z)-level one can realize arbitrary analytic (Z) over a fixed (S), so attacks that try to kill the nonmixed branch from the planar derivative geometry of (S) alone cannot work. \] \item consequently, for every analytic forcing \(G:I\to\mathbf C\), there exists an analytic function \(u_5\) on \(I\) such that \[ \mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}=G; \] \item equivalently, for every analytic forcing \(R:I\to\mathbf C\), there exists an analytic function \(u_5\) on \(I\) such that \[ \mathcal R=R. \] \end{enumerate} In particular, at the current source-level ratio/Wronskian/\(4\times4\)-determinant level, the zero set, parity, and odd/even vanishing pattern of \(\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}\) and \(\mathcal R\) are formally unconstrained. \end{proposition} \begin{proof} Expand the \(4\times4\) Wronskian along the \(u_5\)-column. Since the highest derivative of \(u_5\) appearing in \(W(c,v_5,\lambda,u_5)\) is \(u_5'''\), with coefficient exactly \[ W(c,v_5,\lambda)=J_\lambda, \] there exist analytic coefficients \(a_0,a_1,a_2\) on \(I\) such that \[ W(c,v_5,\lambda,u_5) = J_\lambda\,u_5'''+a_2u_5''+a_1u_5'+a_0u_5. \] Because \(J_\lambda\neq 0\) on \(I\), this is a third-order linear analytic ODE for \(u_5\) with nonvanishing leading coefficient. Standard analytic ODE existence therefore gives an analytic solution \(u_5\) on \(I\) for every analytic forcing \(F\). This proves (1). For (2), given analytic \(G\), set \[ F:=\frac{G}{M}. \] Since \(M\neq 0\) on \(I\), \(F\) is analytic. By (1), choose \(u_5\) such that \[ W(c,v_5,\lambda,u_5)=F. \] Then Proposition~\ref{prop:source-level-Wronskian-lifts-to-4x4} gives \[ \mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}} = M\,W(c,v_5,\lambda,u_5) = G. \] For (3), given analytic \(R\), set \[ G:=\frac{M J_\lambda^2}{c^2}\,R. \] Since \(c\neq 0\), \(M\neq 0\), and \(J_\lambda\neq 0\) on \(I\), this is analytic. By (2), choose \(u_5\) such that \(\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}=G\). Then Proposition~\ref{prop:source-level-Wronskian-nonmixed-four-point} gives \[ \mathcal R = \frac{c^2}{M}\frac{\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}}{J_\lambda^2} = \frac{c^2}{M}\frac{G}{J_\lambda^2} = R. \qedhere \] \end{proof} \begin{remark}[Ceiling of the current source-level reduction] \label{rem:ceiling-of-current-source-level-reduction} Propositions~\ref{prop:source-level-Wronskian-lifts-to-4x4} and \ref{prop:source-level-Wronskian-package-not-enough} show that the current source-level reduction has been pushed to its natural ceiling. The nonmixed \(4\)-point branch is indeed equivalent to an odd-zero problem for the gauge-invariant source-level Wronskian \[ \mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}, \] and even to the \(4\times4\) Wronskian \(W(c,v_5,\lambda,u_5)\). But at that level the odd-zero pattern is still formally free. Accordingly, the missing ingredient can no longer be a generic Wronskian or determinant argument. It must be a genuine \emph{source-coupling theorem}: one that uses additional identities coming from the actual RH source structure to show that the analytically possible \(u_5\)-freedom exhibited above is not realizable on a genuine opened nonmixed arc. \end{remark} ``` ## 2) Replace the entire current block ```latex \begin{remark}[What remains on the nonmixed $4$-point side] \label{rem:what-remains-nonmixed-after-R-zero-bridge} ... \end{remark} ``` with this updated version: ```latex \begin{remark}[What remains on the nonmixed $4$-point side] \label{rem:what-remains-nonmixed-after-R-zero-bridge} The preceding results now give a full local derivative-side picture of the nonmixed exact-contact geometry. \]

Here is an explicit normalized polynomial model showing that this level-set geometry can occur with **exactly two simple odd zeros of (\mathcal R)** and with a **nondegenerate rooted critical pair**.

Work on the normalized interval ([a,x]=[0,1]), with
[
S(t)=t^2,
\qquad
\Gamma_a=D_a,
]
and prescribe
[
\mathcal R(t):=5t^3+5t^2-7t+1.
]
This cubic has exactly two simple zeros in ((0,1)), numerically
[
t\approx 0.165726,\qquad t\approx 0.660736,
]
and one third real zero outside the interval, at
[
t\approx -1.826462.
]
So on ([0,1]) the sign pattern is
[
+,-,+,
]
with exactly two odd sign changes.

Now set
[
\mathcal Z(t):=\int_0^t \mathcal R(u),du
========================================

t-\frac72 t^2+\frac53 t^3+\frac54 t^4,
]
so that
[
\mathcal Z'(t)=\mathcal R(t),
\qquad
\mathcal Z(0)=0.
]
Choose any analytic (\widetilde Y) with
[
\frac12,\widetilde Y''=\mathcal Z,
]
equivalently
[
\widetilde Y''(t)=2\mathcal Z(t).
]
Then, exactly as in the normalized draft formulas, the rooted critical conditions at the pair ((a,x)=(0,1)) are
[
D_0'(1)=2\int_0^1 s(1-s),\mathcal R(s),ds,
]
and
[
D_0(1)-\mathcal Z(0)=\int_0^1 (1-s)^2,\mathcal R(s),ds.
]
For this (\mathcal R), both moments vanish:
[
\int_0^1 s(1-s),\mathcal R(s),ds=0,
\qquad
\int_0^1 (1-s)^2,\mathcal R(s),ds=0.
]
So
[
D_0'(1)=0,
\qquad
D_0(1)=\mathcal Z(0).
]
That is an exact rooted repeated-source critical pair.

It is also nondegenerate. Indeed,
[
D_0''(1)=2\int_0^1 s^2,\mathcal R(s),ds
=======================================

# 2\cdot\frac{5}{12}

\frac56>0.
]
So the implicit function theorem gives a real-analytic critical branch
[
x=\tau(a)
]
through
[
\tau(0)=1,
\qquad
D_a'(\tau(a))=0,
]
and at the rooted point one gets the stationary-target behavior
[
\tau'(0)=0.
]
Also, since (G(a)=V(a)-\mathcal Z(a)) with (V(a)=D_a(\tau(a))), one has
[

\qquad
G'(0)=-\mathcal R(0)=-1.
]

The level-set recrossing also happens exactly as desired. Since

\begin{proposition}[Discriminant reduction for the moving-shear family]
\label{prop:discriminant-reduction-moving-shear}
Let $J$ be a good nonmixed $v_5$-patch. For $\gamma\in\mathbf R$, set
\[
f_\gamma:=u_5-\gamma\lambda.
\]
Define the sheared discriminant set
\[
\mathcal D:=
\left\{
(a,\gamma,h)\in J\times\mathbf R\times J:
a<h,\ 
D_{f_\gamma}(a,h)=0,\ 
\partial_h D_{f_\gamma}(a,h)=0
\right\}.
\]

Then on the region $a<h$ one has the exact equivalence
\[
(a,\gamma,h)\in\mathcal D
\iff
\gamma=\Psi_a(h),
\qquad
\mathfrak D(a,h)=0.
\]
Equivalently,
\[
\mathcal D
=
\left\{
(a,\Psi_a(h),h):\ a<h,\ \mathfrak D(a,h)=0
\right\}.
\]

In particular, on a nonmixed patch the sheared discriminant is not an
independent two-dimensional catastrophe surface in $(a,\gamma,h)$-space:
it is the graph of the repeated-source critical locus
\[
\mathfrak D(a,h)=0
\]
in the extra $\gamma$-direction.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
By Proposition~\ref{prop:source-determinant-form-odd-zero-unrooted-defect}(2),
for every $(a,h)$ with $a<h$ one has
\[
D_{f_\gamma}(a,h)
=
D_\lambda(a,h)\bigl(\Psi_a(h)-\gamma\bigr).
\]
Differentiating in $h$ gives
\[
\partial_h D_{f_\gamma}(a,h)
=
\partial_h D_\lambda(a,h)\bigl(\Psi_a(h)-\gamma\bigr)
+
D_\lambda(a,h)\,\partial_h\Psi_a(h).
\]

On a good nonmixed patch,
\[
D_\lambda(a,h)\neq 0
\qquad (a<h).
\]
Therefore
\[
D_{f_\gamma}(a,h)=0
\iff
\gamma=\Psi_a(h).
\]
At such a point the first term in the formula for $\partial_h D_{f_\gamma}$
vanishes, so
\[
\partial_h D_{f_\gamma}(a,h)=0
\iff
D_\lambda(a,h)\,\partial_h\Psi_a(h)=0
\iff
\partial_h\Psi_a(h)=0.
\]
Finally, by
Remark~\ref{rem:source-determinant-reformulation-Gammaa},
\[
\partial_h\Psi_a(h)
=
\frac{W_h(c,v_5)(a)\,\mathfrak D(a,h)}{D_\lambda(a,h)^2},
\]
and the prefactor is nonvanishing on the nonmixed patch. Hence
\[
\partial_h\Psi_a(h)=0
\iff
\mathfrak D(a,h)=0.
\]
Combining the two equivalences proves the result.
\end{proof}

\begin{proposition}[Generic rooted discriminant point is a transverse crossing]
\label{prop:generic-rooted-discriminant-point-transverse-crossing}
In the setting of
Proposition~\ref{prop:discriminant-reduction-moving-shear},
define the RH-selected slice
\[
\mathcal S_{\mathrm{RH}}
:=
\left\{
(a,\gamma,h)\in J\times\mathbf R\times J:
\gamma=\mathcal Z(x(a))
\right\}.
\]

Let
\[
(a_*,\gamma_*,h_*)\in \mathcal D\cap \mathcal S_{\mathrm{RH}}
\]
and assume
\[
\partial_h^2 D_{f_{\gamma_*}}(a_*,h_*)\neq 0,
\qquad
\mathcal R(x(a_*))\neq 0.
\]
Then there is a neighborhood of $(a_*,\gamma_*,h_*)$ in which
$\mathcal D$ is a unique real-analytic curve
\[
a\longmapsto \bigl(a,\gamma(a),h(a)\bigr),
\]
with
\[
\gamma(a)=\Psi_a(h(a)).
\]

Moreover one has
\[
\gamma'(a_*)=0,
\qquad
h'(a_*)=0,
\]
and
\[
\frac{d}{da}\Bigl(\gamma(a)-\mathcal Z(x(a))\Bigr)\Big|_{a=a_*}
=
-\mathcal R(x(a_*))\,x'(a_*)\neq 0.
\]
Hence the discriminant curve $\mathcal D$ meets the RH-selected slice
$\mathcal S_{\mathrm{RH}}$ transversely at $(a_*,\gamma_*,h_*)$.

In fact the $\gamma$-projection of the discriminant curve has a nondegenerate
local extremum there:
\[
\gamma''(a_*)
=
-\frac{2\,x'(a_*)^2}{x(h_*)-x(a_*)}\,\mathcal R(x(a_*)).
\]
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
By Proposition~\ref{prop:discriminant-reduction-moving-shear},
the discriminant is cut out by
\[
\partial_h\Psi_a(h)=0,
\qquad
\gamma=\Psi_a(h).
\]
At the given point,
\[
\partial_h^2 D_{f_{\gamma_*}}(a_*,h_*)\neq 0.
\]
Since
\[
D_{f_\gamma}(a,h)=D_\lambda(a,h)\bigl(\Psi_a(h)-\gamma\bigr),
\]
differentiating twice in $h$ and evaluating at a discriminant point gives
\[
\partial_h^2 D_{f_{\gamma_*}}(a_*,h_*)
=
D_\lambda(a_*,h_*)\,\partial_h^2\Psi_{a_*}(h_*).
\]
Because $D_\lambda(a_*,h_*)\neq 0$, this implies
\[
\partial_h^2\Psi_{a_*}(h_*)\neq 0.
\]
So by the implicit function theorem there is a unique real-analytic function
\[
h=h(a)
\]
with
\[
h(a_*)=h_*,
\qquad
\partial_h\Psi_a(h(a))=0.
\]
Setting
\[
\gamma(a):=\Psi_a(h(a))
\]
gives the asserted local parametrization of $\mathcal D$.

Now pass to the local normalized nonmixed $x$-coordinate and write
\[
\alpha:=x(a),
\qquad
\tau(\alpha):=x(h(a)),
\qquad
V(\alpha):=D_\alpha(\tau(\alpha)).
\]
By Remark~\ref{rem:source-determinant-reformulation-Gammaa},
\[
\gamma(a)=\Psi_a(h(a))=V(\alpha).
\]
Since $(a_*,\gamma_*,h_*)\in\mathcal S_{\mathrm{RH}}$, one has
\[
V(\alpha_*)=\mathcal Z(\alpha_*),
\qquad
\alpha_*:=x(a_*).
\]

By Proposition~\ref{prop:transport-equations-repeated-source-critical-branch},
at a rooted noncollapse point one has
\[
V'(\alpha_*)=0,
\qquad
\tau'(\alpha_*)=0.
\]
Therefore
\[
\gamma'(a_*)
=
V'(\alpha_*)\,x'(a_*)
=
0,
\]
and
\[
x'(h_*)\,h'(a_*)
=
\tau'(\alpha_*)\,x'(a_*)
=
0,
\]
hence
\[
h'(a_*)=0.
\]

For the transverse-crossing derivative, differentiate
\[
\gamma(a)-\mathcal Z(x(a))
=
V(\alpha)-\mathcal Z(\alpha)
\]
to get
\[
\frac{d}{da}\Bigl(\gamma(a)-\mathcal Z(x(a))\Bigr)
=
x'(a)\bigl(V'(\alpha)-\mathcal R(\alpha)\bigr).
\]
At $a=a_*$, since $V'(\alpha_*)=0$, this becomes
\[
\frac{d}{da}\Bigl(\gamma(a)-\mathcal Z(x(a))\Bigr)\Big|_{a=a_*}
=
-\mathcal R(\alpha_*)\,x'(a_*),
\]
which is nonzero by hypothesis. This proves transversality.

Finally, differentiate
\[
V'(\alpha)=\frac{2}{\tau(\alpha)-\alpha}\bigl(V(\alpha)-\mathcal Z(\alpha)\bigr)
\]
from
Proposition~\ref{prop:transport-equations-repeated-source-critical-branch}(1).
At the rooted point,
\[
V(\alpha_*)-\mathcal Z(\alpha_*)=0,
\qquad
\tau'(\alpha_*)=0,
\]
so
\[
V''(\alpha_*)
=
\frac{2}{\tau(\alpha_*)-\alpha_*}\bigl(V'(\alpha_*)-\mathcal R(\alpha_*)\bigr)
=
-\frac{2}{\tau(\alpha_*)-\alpha_*}\,\mathcal R(\alpha_*).
\]
Hence
\[
\gamma''(a_*)
=
V''(\alpha_*)\,x'(a_*)^2
=
-\frac{2\,x'(a_*)^2}{x(h_*)-x(a_*)}\,\mathcal R(x(a_*)),
\]
as claimed.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[What the discriminant/catastrophe route actually reduces to]
\label{rem:what-discriminant-catastrophe-route-actually-reduces-to}
The discriminant reformulation sharpens the geometry, but it also shows the
limit of purely local catastrophe arguments on this route.

Indeed, by
Proposition~\ref{prop:discriminant-reduction-moving-shear},
the sheared discriminant on a nonmixed patch is already one-dimensional:
it is the graph of the repeated-source critical locus
\[
\mathfrak D(a,h)=0
\]
in the $\gamma$-direction. And by
Proposition~\ref{prop:generic-rooted-discriminant-point-transverse-crossing},
a generic rooted point is not a tangential meeting of sheets, nor a local
fold/cusp obstruction for the RH-selected slice
\[
\gamma=\mathcal Z(x(a)).
\]
It is a \emph{transverse crossing} of a smooth discriminant curve by that
moving slice, with oriented crossing sign controlled by
\[
-\mathcal R(x(a_*)).
\]

Accordingly, the discriminant/catastrophe route does not reduce the adjacent
odd-zero problem to a local singularity classification in
$(a,\gamma,h)$-space. The remaining issue is global: to exclude the existence
of such a transverse crossing along the continued born branch before the
segment exits the arc, collapses affine-planarly, or acquires the next odd
zero of $\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}$.
\end{remark}



Why I think this is the right output from route 2:

* it gives a real structural simplification,
* it explains why “catastrophe” language is mostly misleading here,
* and it isolates the true remaining content: not local singularity theory, but a global no-crossing theorem for the moving slice against a smooth discriminant curve.

That is probably the cleanest honest result available from this line right now.

Dfγ(a,h)=Dλ(a,h)(Ψa(h)−γ),
Dfγ​​(a,h)=Dλ​(a,h)(Ψa​(h)−γ),

∂hDfγ(a,h)=0  ⟺  ∂hΨa(h)=0  ⟺  D(a,h)=0,
∂h​Dfγ​​(a,h)=0⟺∂h​Ψa​(h)=0⟺D(a,h)=0,

the discriminant collapses to the graph
D={(a,Ψa(h),h): D(a,h)=0}.

So the RH-selected condition γ=Z(x(a))γ=Z(x(a)) is not meeting a sheet; it is meeting a 1-dimensional analytic curve. And at a generic rooted point, that meeting is transverse, not tangential. That kills the hope for a local fold/cusp contradiction from bare catastrophe theory.

I also think the transport identities in the companion note sharpen the same picture in exactly the right way. Along a continued critical branch, the rooted defect
G(a)=Ψa(σ(a))−Z(a)

satisfies
G′(a)=2τ(a)−aG(a)−R(a),

so at a first rooted point a∗a∗​ one gets
G′(a∗)=−R(a∗),τ′(a∗)=0,
G′(a∗​)=−R(a∗​),τ′(a∗​)=0,

and, generically, the moving-shear zero set is a genuine fold in (a,t)(a,t)-space. Combined with the fixed-level sheared nonrecurrence theorem, this shows that any nondegenerate first rooted point must occur beyond the maximal fixed-γγ slope-overlap chamber. So the remaining issue is not local singularity, but a post-boundary-exit moving-shear exclusion problem.

The second block — the “adjacent-odd-zero entrance is not a rooted discriminant point” proposition — also looks like a real gain. any other ideas? is there anyway to combine these dead routes in to something we are missing

Yes. I think there are two hybrid routes that are still genuinely alive, and both combine the “dead” routes in a way that adds structure they were each missing alone. The recent notes make that pretty clear: pure level-set topology is too weak, pure fixed-γγ sheared nonrecurrence is too weak, pure catastrophe theory is too weak, and pure planar branch provenance is too weak. The missing ingredient has to remember source-level coupling or global crossing geometry.
1. Recast the moving-shear family as a single third-order ODE family and try a disconjugacy / ECT theorem

This is the one I find most promising.

On a nonmixed arc, define the third-order operator
L[y]:=W(c,v5,λ,y)Jλ.
L[y]:=Jλ​W(c,v5​,λ,y)​.

Because Jλ≠0Jλ​=0 there, this is a well-defined linear analytic differential operator of order 33. The key point is:

    L[c]=L[v5]=L[λ]=0L[c]=L[v5​]=L[λ]=0,

    and for the source-pinned shear family
    fa:=u5−Z(a)λ,
    fa​:=u5​−Z(a)λ,

    one has
    L[fa]=L[u5],
    L[fa​]=L[u5​],

    because L[λ]=0L[λ]=0.

So all the sheared functions fafa​ solve the same inhomogeneous third-order ODE. The only thing that changes with aa is the boundary data.

That is a real structural gain the previous routes were not using.

Why it matters:

A rooted event for the moving-shear family is exactly a repeated-node boundary event for a solution of this same ODE:
Jfa(a)=0,Dfa(a,h)=0,∂hDfa(a,h)=0.
Jfa​​(a)=0,Dfa​​(a,h)=0,∂h​Dfa​​(a,h)=0.

That is essentially a three-point boundary-value problem for solutions of L[y]=L[u5]L[y]=L[u5​].

So the next theorem target becomes:

    Prove that LL is disconjugate / ECT / sign-regular on opened nonmixed arcs, or that its Green kernel has a one-sign property, strong enough to exclude a solution of L[y]=L[u5]L[y]=L[u5​] from satisfying the repeated-node boundary conditions above unless fa≡0fa​≡0 locally, i.e. collapse.

Why this combines the dead routes in a nontrivial way:

    it uses the source-level 4×44×4 Wronskian route, but not just as a free scalar — it uses it as an operator;

    it uses the moving-shear family, but not just as a changing level — it recognizes that the family lives inside one fixed ODE;

    it uses provenance, because the family fafa​ is not arbitrary; it is a very special one-parameter subfamily of solutions with forcing fixed and only the λλ-component moving.

This is the cleanest “structural RH” route I can see right now.

What I would attack concretely:

    write LL explicitly in normalized source coordinates;

    test whether (c,v5,λ)(c,v5​,λ) already form an ECT / Chebyshev system on opened nonmixed arcs;

    if yes, try to show the inhomogeneous equation inherits a no-repeated-node-tangency principle;

    if not globally, try it at least on the adjacent-two-odd-zero chamber.

2. Treat the remaining problem as a global crossing-number theorem for the moving slice against the 1D discriminant curve

The discriminant work killed the naive catastrophe picture, but it also simplified the geometry: the discriminant is a curve, not a surface. That is useful.

You now know:

    the discriminant is
    D={(a,Ψa(h),h): D(a,h)=0},
    D={(a,Ψa​(h),h): D(a,h)=0},

    a generic rooted point is a transverse crossing of this curve by the RH-selected slice
    γ=Z(x(a)),
    γ=Z(x(a)),

    the entrance into the adjacent-two-odd-zero chamber is not already a rooted point,

    and the first rooted point, if it exists, is a stationary target / fold-type event for the moving branch.

So the next theorem could be:

    Prove that along the continued born branch, the RH-selected slice cannot have its first transverse crossing with the discriminant curve before the adjacent-odd-zero connection completes or collapse occurs.

This is not local catastrophe theory anymore. It is a global oriented crossing theorem.

What extra structure might make it work:

    the sign of the rooted defect
    G(a)=Ψa(σ(a))−Z(a),
    G(a)=Ψa​(σ(a))−Z(a),

    and its ODE
    G′(a)=2L(a)G(a)−R(a);
    G′(a)=L(a)2​G(a)−R(a);

    the fact that at a rooted point,
    G′(a∗)=−R(a∗),τ′(a∗)=0;
    G′(a∗​)=−R(a∗​),τ′(a∗​)=0;

    fixed-γγ nonrecurrence, which says the moving crossing can only happen after boundary exit of the frozen chamber;

    and the entry-point no-go, which says it cannot happen at adjacent-zero entry.

So the remaining window is a very specific open interval in parameter space. A good next attack is to show the oriented difference
H(a):=γdisc(a)−Z(x(a))
H(a):=γdisc​(a)−Z(x(a))

cannot change sign there, or must change sign an even number of times, or that a first sign change would force impossible endpoint behavior.

Why this combines the dead routes usefully:

    it uses the discriminant curve,

    it uses the moving-shear provenance,

    it uses the transport/fold formulas,

I attacked it, and the honest result is a **no-go refinement**, not an exclusion theorem.

The key point is: with the current normalized scalar machinery, the exactly-two-odd-zero first-fold configuration is still **formally realizable**. What the attack does give is a sharper statement of what must still be excluded.

Take the normalized nonmixed chart
[
S(x)=x^2
]
and define
[
\mathcal Z(x):=x\Bigl(x-\frac{18-3\sqrt6}{10}\Bigr)\Bigl(x-\frac{18+3\sqrt6}{10}\Bigr)
======================================================================================

x^3-\frac{18}{5}x^2+\frac{27}{10}x.
]
Then
[
\mathcal R(x)=\mathcal Z'(x)=3x^2-\frac{36}{5}x+\frac{27}{10},
]
so (\mathcal R) has exactly two simple zeros,
[
\xi_1=\frac65-\frac{3\sqrt6}{10},
\qquad
\xi_2=\frac65+\frac{3\sqrt6}{10},
]
both lying in ((0,3)).

Now fix the anchor (a=0). One checks directly that
[
\int_0^3 \mathcal Z(u),du=0,
\qquad
\int_0^3 (3-u)\mathcal Z(u),du=0.
]
So with the frozen level (\gamma=\mathcal Z(0)=0), the pair ((0,3)) is a rooted sheared repeated-node point:
[
D_0'(3)=0,
\qquad
D_0(3)=\mathcal Z(0)=0.
]

In fact here
[
D_0(x)=\frac{x(x-3)^2}{10},
]
hence
[
D_0'(x)=\frac{3x^2-12x+9}{10},
]
so the two critical points are
[
x=1,\qquad x=3.
]
The outer one (x=3) is rooted, while the inner one (x=1) is not:
[
D_0(1)=\frac25\neq 0.
]

Moreover this rooted point is nondegenerate in exactly the sense of the current transport/fold package:
[
\mathcal R(0)=\frac{27}{10}\neq 0,
\qquad
\mathcal Z(3)-\mathcal Z(0)=\frac{27}{10}\neq 0.
]
So the first-root formulas would give
[
G'(0)=-\mathcal R(0)=-\frac{27}{10},
\qquad
\tau'(0)=0,
\qquad
\tau''(0)=-1
]
along the outer critical branch.

This matters because it shows the following.

There is an explicit analytic normalized model in which:

* the segment contains **exactly two odd zeros** of (\mathcal R);
* there is a **nondegenerate rooted fold**;
* and there is also a distinct inner critical point that stays unrooted.

So the present scalar package does **not** force a contradiction in the exactly-two-odd-zero case.

What it does show, very sharply, is that the remaining issue is now a **branch-selection problem**.

In this model, the two critical branches are
[
\tau_\pm(a)=2-\frac{2a}{3}\pm \frac13\sqrt{(3-a)(5a+3)}.
]
The lower branch (\tau_-) is the one that comes out of the first odd zero:
[
\tau_-(\xi_1)=\xi_1.
]
It is the “born” inner branch. The upper branch (\tau_+) is the outer one, and at (a=0) it gives the rooted fold:
[
\tau_+(0)=3.
]

So the actual unresolved theorem is no longer “exclude exactly two odd zeros” in the abstract. It is:

[
\boxed{
\textbf{born-branch separation theorem:}
\text{ the analytic continuation of the branch born at the first odd zero cannot transfer}
\
\text{to the outer critical branch before rooting.}
}
]

That is the real content of the attack.

So my verdict is:

* **No**, the current transport + fold + sheared-moment identities do not exclude the exactly-two-odd-zero first fold.
* **Yes**, they reduce the remaining problem to something more specific:

> prove that the **born inner critical branch** cannot jump onto the **outer rooted branch** in the two-odd-zero regime.

That is a much narrower target than before.

The clean next attack would be to look for an invariant that distinguishes the inner and outer critical branches and is preserved under continuation from the seeding odd zero. Candidates would be:
[
\operatorname{sgn}(\tau(a)-r_2(a)),
\quad
\text{or a source-determinant sign/orientation index,}
]
or some monotone quantity attached specifically to the born branch.

So the branch is not dead, but the broad scalar route is basically exhausted. The remaining work is a **branch-label / continuation invariant**, not another kernel-moment identity.

What I would attack next

I would stop looking for more scalar moment identities. As you say, that lane is basically exhausted. The next live object has to be a branch label or continuation invariant that distinguishes the inner branch from the outer one and is preserved under continuation from the seed.

Three candidates seem worth trying.
1. An orientation/sign index from the transport system

Along a critical branch x=τ(a)x=τ(a), you already have
G(a)=Da(τ(a))−Z(a),G′(a)=2τ(a)−aG(a)−R(a),
G(a)=Da​(τ(a))−Z(a),G′(a)=τ(a)−a2​G(a)−R(a),

and, away from collapse,
τ′(a)=G(a)Z(τ(a))−Da(τ(a)).
τ′(a)=Z(τ(a))−Da​(τ(a))G(a)​.

So a natural label is the sign pair
sgn⁡G(a),sgn⁡(Z(τ(a))−Da(τ(a))),
sgnG(a),sgn(Z(τ(a))−Da​(τ(a))),

or equivalently the sign of τ′(a)τ′(a).

Your explicit model suggests the inner branch and the outer rooted branch sit in different sign/orientation classes. If one of those classes is preserved along the born continuation until a true singular event occurs, that could forbid the transfer.
2. A branch-ordering invariant relative to the zeros of RR

This is the candidate you already pointed to, and I think it is promising.

Let r2(a)r2​(a) denote the second zero / second return point / outer level-set branch inside the active two-odd-zero chamber. Then try to track
sgn⁡(τ(a)−r2(a)).
sgn(τ(a)−r2​(a)).

The born inner branch should begin on one side of this separator. The outer rooted branch lies on the other. If you can show that the continued born branch cannot cross the separator without violating one of the already-proved nondegeneracy or one-sign-change chamber facts, that gives the separation theorem directly.
3. A genuinely source-level branch label

This is probably the deepest and most promising if the first two stall.

At source level, the critical branch is really
D(a,h)=0or equivalently∂hΨa(h)=0.
D(a,h)=0or equivalently∂h​Ψa​(h)=0.

So try to find a sign/orientation invariant built from
Dλ(a,h),Du5(a,h),D(a,h),
Dλ​(a,h),Du5​​(a,h),D(a,h),

or from the source-pinned shear
fa=u5−Z(a)λ,
fa​=u5​−Z(a)λ,

that distinguishes the born branch from the outer rooted one and cannot change sign under continuation.

That would be the most RH-specific version of the branch-label idea.
My honest updated view

So I think the situation is now:

    not “exclude two odd zeros”;

    not “find another scalar integral identity”;

    but rather:

find a continuation invariant that separates the born branch from the outer rooted branch.
find a continuation invariant that separates the born branch from the outer rooted branch.​

That is the cleanest next attack I see.

And I do think your counterexample is worth preserving in the draft, at least as a no-go remark, because it prevents the paper from overclaiming that the current transport/fold package already kills the two-odd-zero case.
